The Definite Article in Science Names: Not Proof of Genericity
Responding to objections that the definite article in science names indicates genericity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that the definite article can enter descriptive proper nouns for beautification (tahsin), and evaluate why it does not prove a word is a generic noun (ism jins).

Core Idea
The definite article on proper names is for beautification, not indication of generic meaning.

This passage addresses a key usul point: does the presence of alif lam in names of sciences (e.g., al-fiqh) prove they are generic nouns? The author rebuts objections from Ibn al-Humam and Sayyid Zahid, and presents the correct Hanafi position using the hadith of al-Hasan and al-Husayn and the names of heavenly books. Understanding this helps distinguish between generic nouns and descriptive proper nouns in usul analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed claim
Read the beginning of the passage: the issue is whether the definite article in names of sciences proves they are generic nouns (ism jins).
The claim is that 'alif lam' is a sign of genericity.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that the definite article can enter descriptive proper nouns (a'lam wasfiyyah) for beautification, so it does not prove genericity.
This is supported by the hadith and examples of heavenly books.
3
Examine Ibn al-Humam's objection
Ibn al-Humam objected that the discussion should be limited to the specific name 'usul al-fiqh'. The author responds that the discussion is general, covering all science names.
4
Examine Sayyid Zahid's objection
Sayyid Zahid claimed that using the definite article with science names is a later innovation by non-eloquent speakers. The author refutes this by noting that the names of heavenly books (al-Qur'an, etc.) have the definite article despite being supremely eloquent.
5
Apply the core proof
The hadith 'al-Hasan wa al-Husayn...' demonstrates that alif lam enters proper names for beautification. Therefore, science names like 'al-fiqh' may be descriptive proper nouns, not generic nouns.
This is the decisive evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسرے علوم کا جنس ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔
جواب : بعض شارحین مسلم نے امام ابن الہام پر رد کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ ان کا یہ اعتراض اس وفقیت تام ہوگا جب خاص اصول الفقہ کے اسم جنس ہونے پر کلام کا مدار ہو حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہو بلکہ کلام تو مطلقاً اسامی علوم کے بارے میں ہے لہذا ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ مستدل کا مقصود یہ ہو کہ بعض علوم کے اسامی پر بحیثیت جنس الف ولام داخل ہوتے ہیں جیسے انو ، الصرف الفقہ وغیر ھا۔
سید زاهد كا اعتراض : سید زاہد ہروی نے یہاں یہ کلام کیا ہے کہ اسماء علوم الفلام کا دخول ان مولدین کے کلام میں حادث ہوا ہے جو فصاحت سے نابلد ہیں مگر وہ جو فصحاء ہیں تو ان کے کلام میں ایسا نہیں پایا جا تا ۔
جواب : یہ قول بھی مردود ہے اس لئے کہ اسماء کتب سماویہ جیسے القرآن، الانجیل الزبور، التوریت پر الف ولام داخل ہے باوجود یکہ وہ کتابیں بالا جماع فصاحت و بلاغت کے حد اعجاز تک پہونچی ہوئی ہیں ۔ جواب باصواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ اسم جنس کے علاوہ اعلام وصفیہ پر بھی تحسین کے لئے لام کا دخول فصیح صحیح اور شائع و ذائع ہے چنانچہ حدیث شریف میں ہے الحسن والحسین سید اشباب اهل الجنة یونہی ادنی مناسبت کے سبب سے معنی علمیت باقی رکھتے ہوئے علم کی اضافت بھی صحیح ہے جیسے عمرنا او عمر الذى هو سيدنا وترجو مدده في كل حال من الاحوال - بلکہ اگر معنی علمیت سے خالی کر لیا جائے تو علم کے مضاف ہونے میں کوئی کلام ہی نہیں فلہذا دخول الف لام کا اور لحوق اضافت دلیل جنسیت نہیں ہو سکتی۔
The genericity of other sciences is not proven. Response: Some commentators of Muslim have rebutted Ibn al-Humam saying that his objection would be completely applicable only if the discussion revolves around the name 'usul al-fiqh' being a generic noun, but that is not the case. Rather, the discussion is generally about the names of sciences. Hence, it is possible that the arguer's intention is that the definite article enters some science names as a generic noun, such as 'al-nahw', 'al-sarf', 'al-fiqh', etc. Objection of Sayyid Zahid: Sayyid Zahid Harawi said here that the entry of the definite article into the names of sciences occurs in the speech of later scholars (mawalidin) who are not fluent in eloquence. But among the eloquent (fuhaha'), it is not found in their speech. Response: This statement is also rejected because the names of heavenly books such as 'al-Qur'an', 'al-Injil', 'al-Zabur', 'al-Tawrat' have the definite article, despite these books, by consensus, reaching the peak of eloquence and rhetoric. The correct answer: It is that besides generic nouns, the entry of lam for beautification into descriptive proper nouns is eloquent, correct, and widespread. Thus, in the noble hadith: 'Al-Hasan and al-Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise.' Similarly, due to a slight appropriateness, while preserving the meaning of properness, the addition (idafah) of the name of the science is also correct, like 'Nahwuna' or 'al-Nahw alladhi huwa sayyiduna wa narju maddahu fi kulli hal min al-ahwal'. Rather, if it is stripped of the meaning of properness, then there is no argument about the name being in idafah. Hence, the entry of the definite article and the occurrence of idafah cannot be proof of genericity.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a dispute about whether the presence of the definite article (alif lam) in the names of sciences (e.g., al-fiqh, al-nahw) indicates that these names are generic nouns (ism jins). The text presents and rebuts two objections. The first is from Ibn al-Humam, who supposedly argued that his objection would apply specifically if the discussion were about 'usul al-fiqh' being a generic noun, but the text clarifies that the discussion is general. The second objection is from Sayyid Zahid Harawi, who claimed that using the definite article with science names is a later innovation by non-eloquent speakers. This is refuted by noting that the names of the divinely revealed books (al-Qur'an, etc.) bear the definite article despite being at the peak of eloquence. The correct answer is that the definite article can enter descriptive proper nouns (a'lam wasfiyyah) for beautification (tahsin), as seen in the hadith 'al-Hasan wa al-Husayn...'. Additionally, one can say 'nahwuna' (our nahw) while still preserving the properness, or even strip it of properness and use it in idafah. Therefore, the definite article and idafah are not proof that these names are generic nouns.

Key Terms
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that denotes a category or genus, not a specific individual.
علم وصفی (‘alam wasfi): A descriptive proper noun, i.e., a name that originally describes but is used as a proper name (e.g., al-Hasan).
تحسین (tahsin): Beautification; the use of the definite article for aesthetic or rhetorical enhancement rather than to indicate definiteness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because 'al-Qur'an' is not a science name.
C) Because alif lam cannot enter proper nouns.
D) Because the Qur'an has no definite article in original Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The definite article in names of sciences does not prove genericity; it may enter for beautification in descriptive proper nouns, as shown by the hadith and names of heavenly books.

Science Names as Generic Proper Nouns (Usul Definition)
Defining 'ilm jins via mental unity and disputing the author's necessity argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'ilm jins (generic proper noun) and apply the criterion of mental unity to distinguish it from a personal proper noun, using the Hanafi usul framework.

Core Idea
A science name can be proper generically if its meaning has mental unity across individuals.

In Hanafi usul, names of sciences like fiqh and nahw are debated: are they personal proper nouns or generic proper nouns? This passage presents the view that they are generic proper nouns (jins) based on mental unity (wahda dhihniyya). We'll explore the argument, the author's objection, and the commentators' refutation, clarifying how a name can be proper without referring to a single individual.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of mental unity
Recognize that when multiple individuals learn the same science, what is in each mind is called the same name (e.g., fiqh), indicating a common mental identity.
This is the core of the generic proper noun argument.
2
Distinguish personal proper noun from generic proper noun
Contrast a personal proper noun like 'Usama' (referring to one person) with a generic proper noun like 'fiqh' (referring to a shared mental concept across instances).
The author uses the necessity argument to claim that only some words qualify as generic proper nouns.
3
Follow the author's objection from necessity
The author argues that generic properness is only accepted by necessity (dharura) for words that show signs of properness (e.g., non-declinability) but not for science names.
Example: 'Usama' is treated as proper by necessity despite lacking explicit signs.
4
Examine the commentators' meaning-based refutation
The commentators respond that the proponents base their view on meaning, not the word. Authors mentally determine specific sciences and their names, implying a determinate meaning that qualifies for generic properness.
The meaning of a science name has a particularity beyond mere generic unity.
5
Derive the final position
Since the meaning is determined in the mind (ta'ayyun dhihni) and shared across individuals, the name is a generic proper noun, not a personal one. This is the relied-upon view.
This affects how commands using such names are interpreted (e.g., 'learn fiqh' refers to the science, not a specific instance).

Source Text

بعض علماء فن کا قول یہ ہے کہ اسماء علوم علم جنس ہیں اس لئے کہ علوم کے مسمیات یعنی مسائل و احکام کے مابین تعین ذہنی یا وحدت ذهنیہ معتبر ہے کیونکہ فقہ مثلا جب اس کو بہت سارے لوگ حاصل کرتے ہیں تو ان اشخاص کثیرہ میں سے ہر ایک کے ذہن میں جو ہے لامحالہ وہ فقہ ہی ہے پس اگر وحدت معتبر نہ ہو توان اشخاص کے ذہن میں جو علم ہے اس پر فقہ کا اطلاق صحیح نہ ہوگا چنانچہ اسی وجہ سے معلومات مخصوصہ کو علم مخصوص اور الفاظ مخصوصہ اور اس کے معانی کو کتاب مخصوص کہتے ہیں جس طرح ایک لفظ جود و شخص کی زبان سے صادر ہوا یا ایک ہی شخص سے دو وقتوں میں صادر ہوا یا ایک معنی جو دو ذھنوں میں حاصل ہے یا ایک ہی ذہن میں دو وقتوں میں حاصل ہوا ہے تو اسکو لفظ واحد یا معنی واحد ہی کہتے ہیں جس کا مفاد یہ ہے کہ ان مسمیات میں وحدت معتبر ہے مگر چونکہ حال واحد شخصی کا قیام محال متعددہ میں محال ہے اس لئے یہ وحدت وحدت شخصیہ یا تعین شخصی نہیں ہوسکتی ہاں البتہ یہ وحدت و تعین غیر شخصی ذہنی ہے اسلئے ہم نے بلحاظ وحدت ذہنیہ اسکو علم جنس قرار دیا۔ یہ مذہب محقق سید شریف جرحانی ، سید جلال الدین محقق دوانی اور سید زاہد ہروی کا ہے۔
قوله قلنا يثبت بالضرورة ۔ اس عبارت سے حضرت مصنف قائلین اعلام جنسیہ کے خیال کی تردید کرنا چاہتے ہیں۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ بعض الفاظ میں بر بنائے ضرورت علم جنس مان لیا جاتا ہے چونکہ بعض الفاظ میں معارف کی علامتیں پائی جاتی ہیں اور ان کے ساتھ معارف کا سا معاملہ کیا جاتا ہے چنانچہ اس کو مبتد اوذ والحال وغیرہ بناتے ہیں یا ایک سبب کے انضمام و اعتبار کر لینے کے بعد غیر منصرف مانتے ہیں حالانکہ وہ معرفہ نہیں ہوتا اس لئے بر بنائے ضرورت علمیت جنسیہ کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں جیسے عدل تقدیری۔ مثال کے طور پر لفظ اسامہ کو اہل زبان نے دیکھا کہ غیر منصرف مستعمل ہے حالانکہ اسامہ میں سوائے تاء تانیث کے کوئی دلیل اس میں موجود نہیں تو انہوں نے علمیت کا اس میں ضرورۃ اعتبار کر لیا، اس کے برعکس اسمائے علوم میں یہ ضرورت متحقق نہیں اس لئے علم جنس کا اعتبار قطعا مناسب نہیں ۔ مصنف کی تردید: بعض شراح نے مصنف کے خیال مذکور کو ساقط الاعتبار قرار دیتے ہوئے کہا ہے کہ قائلین علم جنس کے خلاف یہ معارضہ اس وقت صحیح ہو گا جب اس کا مدار لفظ پر ہو لیکن اگر مدار معنی پر ہو تو درست نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ہم ان اسماء کے معانی میں ایسی خصوصیت دیکھتے ہیں جو الفاظ معانی کی ذات میں متحقق وحدت نوعی و جنسی سے زائد ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس میں کوئی شبہ نہیں کہ حضرات مصنفین جب کتابوں کی تصنیف کرنے بیٹھتے ہیں تو اولاً اپنے اذھان میں علوم مخصوصہ، ایسے ہی الفاظ مخصوصہ اور اس کے معانی کا استحضار کرتے ہیں پھر ان معلومات موجودہ فی الذہن اور الفاظ و معانی کے مناسبت سے ان علوم کے اسماء اور کتابوں کے ناموں کا انتخاب و تعین کرتے ہیں جس کا صریح مطلب یہ رکھتا ہے کہ وہ معلوم معهود متعین ہوتے ہیں فلھذا اس پر علمیت کا حکم لگانا صحیح ہے تاہم یہ شرکت سے مانع نہیں ہوتا اس لئے علم شخص تو نہیں ہو سکتا لیکن علم جنس ضرور ہو سکتا ہے۔
Some scholars of the art say that the names of sciences are generic nouns (jins) because among the meanings of the sciences, i.e., the issues and rulings, mental determination (ta'ayyun dhihni) or mental unity (wahda dhihniyya) is considered. For example, when many people acquire fiqh, what is in the mind of each of these many individuals is inevitably fiqh. If unity were not considered, then the knowledge in their minds could not correctly be called fiqh. Similarly, specific known things are called a specific science, and specific words and their meanings are called a specific book. Just as a word uttered by the tongue of a generous person, or uttered by the same person at two times, or a meaning that exists in two minds, or exists in one mind at two times, is called a single word or a single meaning. The implication is that unity is considered in these named things. However, since the state of individual unity cannot exist in multiple instances, this unity is not individual unity or personal determination. Rather, it is non-personal mental unity and determination. Therefore, we consider it a generic noun (jins) based on mental unity. This is the school of al-Muhaqqiq Sayyid Sharif al-Jurjani, Sayyid Jalal al-Din al-Muhaqqiq al-Dawani, and Sayyid Zahid al-Harawi.
His statement: 'We say it is established by necessity.' With this phrase, the author intends to refute the view of those who hold that the names are generic proper nouns. The gist is that in some words, generic properness is accepted by necessity because some words have signs of properness (ma'arif) and are treated as proper nouns. For example, they are made mubtada', hal, etc., or are considered non-declinable (ghayr munsarif) after incorporating a cause, even though they are not actually proper nouns. So they accept generic properness by necessity, like 'adl taqdiri'. For example, the people of language saw that the word 'Usama' is used as non-declinable, even though 'Usama' has no sign of properness except the ta' of femininity. So they necessarily accepted properness in it. In contrast, this necessity is not realized in the names of sciences, so considering them generic proper nouns is absolutely inappropriate. Refutation of the author: Some commentators have deemed the author's mentioned view as invalid, saying that this objection against the proponents of generic nouns would be correct if it were based on the word, but if it is based on meaning, it will not be correct. Because we see in the meanings of these names a particularity that exceeds the generic and specific unity inherent in the meanings of words. There is no doubt that when authors sit down to compose books, they first present in their minds the specific sciences, specific words, and their meanings. Then, based on these mentally present known things and the appropriateness of the words and meanings, they choose and determine the names of those sciences and books. This clearly implies that they are known, recognized, and determined. Therefore, applying properness to them is correct. However, this does not prevent sharing (ishtirak), so they cannot be personal proper nouns, but they can certainly be generic proper nouns.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents and discusses the view that the names of sciences (e.g., fiqh, nahw) are generic nouns (jins) based on mental unity. The argument is that when many people know fiqh, what is in each mind is called 'fiqh' because there is a mental unity among those individual instances. This is not a personal unity but a generic mental unity. This view is attributed to al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani, al-Dawani, and al-Harawi. The author (musannif) then rebuts this by saying that in some words, generic properness is accepted by necessity (dharura) due to signs of properness, but this necessity does not exist in science names; hence, considering them generic proper nouns is inappropriate. He gives the example of 'Usama' which is treated as a proper noun by necessity due to its non-declinability, despite lacking obvious properness signs. Some commentators then refute the author, arguing that the author's objection is valid only if based on the word, but the proponents base their view on meaning. They argue that authors mentally determine specific sciences and their names when writing books, implying that these names are known and determined, thus justifying the application of generic properness (but not personal properness). So the final position is that science names can be considered generic proper nouns (jins), not individual proper nouns.

Key Terms
وحدت ذہنیہ (wahda dhihniyya): Mental unity: the common conceptual identity that exists in the minds of multiple individuals when they think of the same science.
تعین ذہنی (ta'ayyun dhihni): Mental determination: the specific, recognized identity of a science or book in the mind of an author prior to naming.
علم جنس (‘ilm jins): A generic proper noun: a name that is proper in the sense of being a known entity, but not limited to a single individual; it denotes a genus with mental unity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentators in the passage, why is the author's objection (that necessity does not apply to science names) invalid?
A) Because the necessity argument is irrelevant to the discussion.
B) Because the proponents base their view on meaning, not word-form.
C) Because the author misunderstood the definition of necessity.
D) Because science names are indeed personal proper nouns.

Key Takeaway
Science names are generic proper nouns because their meanings have mental unity, making them determinate in the mind without being limited to a single instance.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Universality of Subject-Matter: Refuting Objections and Reconciling Definitions
Refuting objections to universal meaning and reconciling views on names of sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi refutation of the claim that non-applicability to parts implies proper nounhood, and apply the four definitions of 'science' to show that names of sciences are universal in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
Non-applicability to parts does not make a term a proper noun—'house', 'four', and 'sikanjabin' are still generic nouns.

In Hanafi usul, the subject matter of a science is often considered a single universal concept. A common objection is that if a term does not apply to its parts, it must be a proper noun. This lesson explores the author's double refutation—general and detailed—using everyday examples. Then, we see how three different definitions of 'science' are reconciled, all preserving its universality. By the end, you'll appreciate the logical rigour of Hanafi usul in defending the generic nature of scientific names.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The opponent argues: if a term (like the name of a science) does not apply to its individual issues (parts), it must be a proper noun (alam shakhs). State this claim clearly.
2
General refutation with 'house'
Analyse the example: 'house' (bayt) is a generic noun by consensus, yet it does not apply to its parts (wall or roof alone). So non-applicability is not sufficient for proper nounhood.
The consensus (ittifaq) that 'house' is a generic noun is key.
3
Detailed refutation with 'four' and 'sikanjabin'
Decompose these compound terms: 'four' is composed of homogeneous units, 'sikanjabin' of heterogeneous parts. Neither applies to its parts, yet they are not proper nouns. This refutes the opponent's objection comprehensively.
Both examples cover the spectrum of composition types.
4
Reconcile definitions of 'science'
Consider the three opinions: science as a collection of issues, as a collection of perceptions, as a disposition (malakah), or as a considerable quantity. Analyse each to show why the term 'science' remains universal under all.
The author shows that even on a personalist view, multiplicity in minds suffices for universality.
5
Derive the conclusion
Conclude that the names of sciences are generic nouns (asmā' ajnās), supporting the author's position. Understand the implication for usul: the subject matter is universal, not proper.

نقض اجمالی ہے۔ دوسر انتقض تفصیلی ہے۔ اپنے قول وفیہ انہ منقوض بالبیت سے نقض اجمالی کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے بیت بالا تفاق اسم جنس ہے علم نہیں ہے کہ اس کا صدق کثیرین پر شرکت سے مانع نہیں ہے، اور اس کے اجزاء سقف و جدار ہیں چونکہ سقف وجدار کے مجموعہ کا نام بیت ہے تا ہم بیت کا صدق صرف جدار پر یا صرف سقف پر درست نہیں چنانچہ تنہا جدار کو یا تنہا سقف کو بیت نہیں کہتے ۔ پس کل کا اپنے جزا پر صادق نہ آنا اگر شخصیہ ہونے کی دلیل ہوتی تو بیت کو علم شخص ہونا چاہئے جبکہ بیت بالا جماع علم شخص نہیں ۔

نقض تفصيلي والحل أن المعنى الكلى الخ سے نقض تفصیلی کی طرف اشارہ ہے ایسا نہیں کہ والحل سے نقض اجمالی کے جواب کی اشارہ ہے جیسا کہ بعض شارحین کو والحل سے وہم ہوا ہے نقض اجمالی کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ کہنا کہ " جس کا صدق بعض پر نہ ہو وہ علم مشخص ہوتا ہے ہم اس پر منع دارد کرتے ہیں وہ اس طرح کے معنی بھی کبھی اجزاء متفقہ سے مرکب ہوتے ہیں جیسے الاربعہ جو چار وحدات سے مرکب ہے اور چاروں وحدات متفق ہیں اور کبھی معنی کلی اجزاء مختلفہ سے مرکب ہوتے ہیں جیسے سکنجبین جو شہد اور سرکہ سے مرکب ہے اور ان کے دونوں اجزاء مختلف ہیں۔ پس بہر دو صورت دونوں کھلی اپنے کسی جز پر صادق نہیں آتی چنانچہ کل واحد اربعہ کے امر فرد واحد کوار بعد اور شہد وسر کہ میں سے ہر ایک کو تیجہین نہیں کہا جاسکتا ۔ حاصل اعتراض یہ کہ معنی کلی کا اپنے جز پر صادق نہ آنا اگر علم شخص ہونے کی دلیل ہوتی تو سنجین اور اربعہ بھی اعلام شخصیہ ہوتے جبکہ سنجین اور الاربعہ کو کوئی لم شخص نہیں کہتا۔ لہذا ہر مسئلہ پر بھی اگر اس فن کا صدق نہ ہوتا ہو تو اس سے اسکا شخصیہ ہونا لازم نہیں بلکہ بیت، اربعہ اور سنجین کی طرح اسم جنس ہی ہوگا علم جنس وعلم شخص نہیں ہو سکتا۔ محاکمه اسماء علوم کے بارے میں تین اقوال مختلفہ کے مابین محاکمہ کرتے ہوئے بعض اہل علم نے کہا ہے کہ ۔ در علم یا تو مجموعہ مسائل سے عبارت ہے اس حیثیت سے کہ اس مجموعہ سے کوئی خارج نہیں ہے یا مجموعہ ادراکات مسائل کا نام ہے اسی حیثیت سے کہ مجموعہ ادراکات میں سے کوئی باہر نہ ہو، یا پھر علیم سے مراد ملکہ ہے یا قدر معتد بہ مسائل ہے جس سے اس علم کی غایت حاصل ہو سکے۔ مذکورہ
چاروں تقادیر پر اسماء علوم کے کلی ہونے میں کوئی شبہ نہیں رہ جاتا ہے اس لئے کہ بر تقدیر اول مجموعہ مسائل گرچہ ایسا امر شخص ہے کہ گھٹ بڑھ نہ سکے تاہم اذہان کے اعتبار سے اس میں تکثر وتعدد ہونا امر مشاہد ہے اور کسی امر شخصی کو کلی ہونے کے لئے فقط اس قدر تکثر کافی ہے۔ یونہی تقدیر دوم پر بھی کلی ہے کیونکہ مجموعه ادراکات مسائل کے افراد وہ علوم ہوتے ہیں جو اذھان کثیرہ میں موجود و ثابت میں اور اس پر کلی صادق آتی ہے۔ تیسری تقدیر پر کی اس لئے ہے کہ ملکہ کے افراد کا تعدد اور پھر اس افراد پر ملکہ کا صدق ملکہ کے کثرت محال کے اعتبار سے ہے اور محال اذھان علماء ہیں۔ اس طرح چوتھی تقدیر پر بھی کلی ہے کیونکہ قدر معتد بہ کے لئے کوئی حد متعین نہیں ہوتی رہے وہ مسائل جو بالفعل مستخرجہ ہیں اس کے لئے بھی کسی حد کا تعین نہیں کیا جا سکتا اس لئے کہ مسائل دن بدن بڑھتے رہتے ہیں۔ الغرض ان محتملات اربہ کی بنیاد پر اسماء علوم اسماء اجناس ہیں اس لئے مصنف کا مذہب حق ہے۔
There is a general refutation and a detailed refutation. His statement 'And in it, that it is refuted by 'house'' indicates the general refutation. Its summary: 'house' is by agreement a generic noun, not a proper noun, because its predication to many does not prevent commonality, and its parts are roof and walls. Since the name 'house' is given to the combination of roof and walls, yet the predication of 'house' is not correct for only a wall or only a roof; thus one does not say 'house' of a wall alone or a roof alone. So if a whole not being true of its part were evidence for its being a proper noun, then 'house' would have to be a proper noun, while 'house' is not a proper noun by agreement. The detailed refutation and the solution: 'And the universal meaning, etc.' indicates the detailed refutation. It is not that 'and the solution' indicates an answer to the general refutation, as some commentators have imagined. The gist of the general refutation is: 'That which is not true of some part is a specific proper noun' — we deny this; such meanings are sometimes composed of homogeneous parts, like 'four' which is composed of four units, and the four units are homogeneous; and sometimes a universal meaning is composed of heterogeneous parts, like 'sikanjabin' which is composed of honey and vinegar, and its two parts are different. So in both cases, the whole is not true of any single part; thus the unit of 'four' is not called 'one individual', nor is each of honey and vinegar called 'sikanjabin'. The objection is: if a universal meaning not being true of its part were evidence for its being a proper noun, then 'sikanjabin' and 'four' would also be proper nouns, while no one says 'sikanjabin' and 'four' are proper nouns. Therefore, for every science, if its name is not true of its issues, it does not necessarily become a proper noun; rather it remains a generic noun like 'house', 'four', and 'sikanjabin'; it cannot be a generic proper noun or a proper noun. Adjudication regarding the names of sciences: Some scholars have adjudicated among three different opinions: A science either is a collection of issues in the sense that nothing external is excluded from that collection, or it is a name for a collection of perceptions of issues in the sense that nothing external is excluded from the collection of perceptions, or 'knowledge' refers to a disposition (malakah), or to a considerable quantity of issues by which the goal of that science can be achieved. In all four estimations, there remains no doubt that the names of sciences are universal. Because in the first estimation, the collection of issues, even though it is a specific thing that cannot increase or decrease, yet in the consideration of minds, multiplicity and diversity occur observably, and this multiplicity is sufficient for a specific thing to be universal. Similarly, in the second estimation, it is universal because the individuals of the collection of perceptions are those sciences that are present and affirmed in many minds, and the universal applies to them. In the third estimation, it is universal because the individuals of the disposition are multiple, and the predication of disposition upon those individuals is due to the multiplicity of the disposition in different loci, and the loci are the minds of scholars. Likewise, in the fourth estimation, it is universal because there is no fixed limit for a considerable quantity; those issues that are actually extracted also cannot be defined by a limit because issues increase day by day. In short, based on these four possibilities, the names of sciences are names of genera, so the author's doctrine is correct.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a usul discipline. It addresses an objection to the claim that the subject matter of a science must be a single universal concept applicable to all its parts. The author refutes the objection in two ways: general and detailed. The general refutation uses the example of 'house' (bayt): it is a generic noun, not a proper noun, yet it does not apply to its parts (walls or roof alone). So non-applicability to parts does not entail proper nounhood. The detailed refutation uses examples like 'four' and 'sikanjabin' (a honey-vinegar drink) to show that even composite terms do not apply to their parts yet remain universal. Then the passage reconciles three or four definitions of 'science' (ilm) and concludes that all these definitions preserve the universal nature of the names of sciences, supporting the author's position that the names of sciences are generic nouns. This analysis is typical of Hanafi usul, emphasizing rational argumentation and detailed refutation of opposing views.

Key Terms
معنی کلی (ma'na kulli): A universal concept that applies to multiple individuals or instances.
علم شخص (alam shakhs): A proper noun that refers to a specific individual, not a class.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that applies to multiple individuals or instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the definitions of 'science' (ilm) considered in the reconciliation?
A) A collection of issues
B) A collection of perceptions
C) A disposition (malakah)
D) A proper noun

Key Takeaway
The names of sciences are universal (generic nouns) because a term's non-application to its parts does not make it proper, as shown by everyday examples.

Basit and Kasb in Nazar: The Role of Tartib
Definitional analysis of basit and kasb in nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why basit cannot be acquired (kasb) under the Hanafi definition of nazar requiring tartib, and identify the verbal nature of the dispute with those who define nazar as mere observation.

Core Idea
Basit cannot be acquired through nazar because kasb requires ordering – and basit has no parts to order.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, ‘nazar’ (speculative reasoning) is the path to acquired knowledge. This lesson unpacks a subtle but critical point: whether simple, partless concepts (basit) can be objects of nazar and thus be acquired. The answer hinges on how we define nazar itself – a definitional dispute that reveals the deep structure of Hanafi legal epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the author is ruling on: the status of basit in relation to kasb (acquisition of knowledge through nazar). The ruling is that basit cannot be kasb under the standard definition of nazar.
This is a usul definition, not a fiqh ruling; the 'ruling' is a conceptual classification.
2
Understand the definition of nazar
The passage presents two definitions: (1) nazar as sequential ordering of known premises (tartib), and (2) nazar as mere observation of the intelligible (mulahaza). Recognize which definition the Hanafi school predominantly adopts.
The author aligns with the tartib definition, which is the majority Hanafi view.
3
Analyze why basit fails the tartib condition
Kasb requires tartib, and tartib requires multiplicity (taddud) – multiple premises to order. Basit, by definition having no parts, lacks this multiplicity. Therefore, basit cannot be the object of kasb in nazar.
The matn's phrase 'la yaqbal al-amal' (does not accept work) refers to the impossibility of ordering.
4
Examine the opposing view
Some scholars (e.g., Taftazani, commentator of al-Mawaqif) define nazar as simple observation. For them, basit can be kasb because no ordering is needed – mere direction of attention suffices.
This view considers definition by simple concepts rationally permissible, though rare.
5
Assess the nature of the disagreement
The author argues the dispute is verbal (lafzi) because it has no practical consequence (thamara). Both sides agree on the substantive point that basit cannot produce knowledge through the standard process of nazar requiring tartib.
Verbal disagreements are not considered harmful in usul; they reflect different terminological choices.

خلاصہ یہ کہ بسیط کے سب ہونے نہ ہونے میں اختلاف لفظی ہے پس جس نے نظر کی تعریف میں دوحرکتیں لازم قرار دی ہیں ان کے نزدیک بلاشبہ ترتیب حرکت ثانیہ کے لوازم میں سے ہوگی لہذاوہ جس میں صرف حرکت واحدہ پائی جائینگی کا سب نہ ہوگا، اس کے برعکس جنہوں نے نظر میں حرکت واحدہ پر اکتفا کیا تو ان کے نزدیک بلاشبہ مجہول کے حاصل ہونے کے لئے حرکت ثانیہ کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے جس کے لئے ترتیب لازم ہے بلکہ ذہن میں مطلوب کے مناسب امر موجود کا لحاظ کرنا حصول مطلوب کے لئے کافی ہے مگر یہ بات پوشیدہ نہیں کہ لفظی اختلاف شان عقلاء سے بعید ہے۔ کیونکہ اس پر کوئی ثمرہ مرتب نہیں ہوتا غالباً اس تفصیل کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے مصنف نے حاشیہ میں کہا ہے۔
" وقول شارح المواقف ان من جوز التعريف بالمعاني البسيطة فله أن يقول أن المعانى البسيطة قد لا تكون ملحوظة قصداً فاذا استحضرت ولوحظت قصداً افادت العلم بالمهية وان كان ذالك نادراً
شارح مواقف کے قول پر مصنف نے متعدد وجوہ سے اعتراض کرتے ہوئے کہا۔
مكابرة مر دودة فان ملاحظة الماهية لا تُسَمَّى كسباً بالاتفاق والالكان التعريف اللفظي تعريفا حقيقياً وكان تذكر النظر مفيداً لعلم جديد الى غير ذالک من المفاسد اللازمة وأن الماهية المعلومة من اللوازم البينة للمعنى البسيط وان كان اللزوم بعد استحضاره فتد برانتهت
عبارت حاشیہ فان ملاحظة الماهیة الخ سے قول شارح مواقف پر پہلا اعتراض وارد ہے۔ اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ملاحظہ کو بالاتفاق "کسب نہیں کہا جاتا کیونکہ اگر ملاحظہ کسب کے ہم معنی ہو تو تعریف لفظی کا تعریف حقیقی ہونا لازم آئے گا اس لئے کہ تعریف لفظی میں حقیقی کی طرح ملاحظہ کا وجود ہوتا ہے۔ پھر اگر نظر میں ملاحظہ معتبر ہو تو لازم آئے گا کہ جب جب نظر کو ذکر کیا جائے تو ہر مرتبہ حد جدید
Those who accept rational obligation responded to the mentioned school by saying that the recited verses, although definitive in their transmission (thubut), their indication of obligation is presumptive (zanni), so it is possible that the command is not for obligation. And the hadith's indication of obligation, even if definitive in indication, the hadith itself is presumptive in transmission because it is a khabar wahid. For this reason, the author did not prove the obligation of nazar from transmitted evidences but proved it with a definitive rational proof, saying 'because it is a prerequisite of the obligatory, and everything upon which the obligatory depends is obligatory.'
His statement: 'The simple (basit) is not a kasib because it does not accept work (amal).'
Basit is a concept that has no parts at all. Therefore, basit cannot be a sabab (means), i.e., from a simple concept one cannot attain knowledge of any single or composite thing, because for kasb (acquisition) the sequential ordering (tartib) of known matters in the first instance is necessary, and ordering requires multiplicity and plurality, whereas basit has no multiplicity. Hence, nazar is not possible in it. The author (matn) pointed to this meaning with his statement 'does not accept work.'
From this, it became clear that the statement of the impossibility of basit being a kasib depends on the consideration of the condition of ordering in the definition of nazar, as the author said that basit does not become a sabab. By kasb is meant the kasb that is considered in the sciences. Since basit does not accept the act of ordering necessary in the syllogism, the absence of kasb does not mean that basit does not acquire at all. Thus, it is transmitted from Shaykh Abu Ali Sina that definition by a simple concept is rare and deficient. However, those who did not consider the condition of ordering in the definition of nazar but defined nazar as 'observation of the intelligible' like the author of al-Tahdhib, Allamah Taftazani, etc., according to them basit is certainly a sabab, because the condition of ordering is not considered in the definition of nazar; rather, mere observation is sufficient. Because based on this view, nazar is the name for directing attention to the simple meaning that is present in the mind. Thus, the commentator of al-Mawaqif said that definition by simple meanings is rationally permissible. Then, there will be a single movement from the sought to the beginning. Then this sought will be obtained in the mind without a second movement for which ordering is necessary. However, definition by simple meanings will not be as precise as definition by composite meanings, nor does it have much involvement in the art and discipline. Therefore, scholars did not pay attention to definition by simple meanings and restricted definition to composite meanings, for this is considered in the acquisition of knowledge.
The summary is that the disagreement about basit being a sabab or not is verbal. So, those who consider two movements necessary in the definition of nazar, according to them ordering will be among the necessities of the second movement; hence, that in which only a single movement is found will not be a sabab. Conversely, those who suffice with a single movement in nazar, according to them the existence of a second movement for which ordering is necessary is not required for obtaining the unknown; rather, considering the existing matter appropriate to the sought in the mind is sufficient for obtaining the sought. But it is not hidden that a verbal disagreement is contrary to the dignity of the intelligent, because no practical consequence results from it. Probably indicating this detail, the author said in the margin:
"And the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif that he who permits definition by simple meanings may say that simple meanings may not be intendedly observed; so when they are present and intendedly observed, they provide knowledge of the essence, although that is rare."
The author objected to the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif in several ways, saying: 'It is a rejected stubbornness, for the observation of the essence is unanimously not called kasb. Otherwise, linguistic definition would become real definition, and mentioning nazar would be beneficial for new knowledge, besides other necessary corruptions. And that the essence known from the evident necessary concomitants of the simple meaning, even if the necessity is after its presence, so reflect.'
The margin text 'for the observation of the essence' etc. presents the first objection to the statement of the commentator of al-Mawaqif. The gist of the objection is that observation (mulahaza) is unanimously not called kasb, because if observation were synonymous with kasb, linguistic definition would necessitate being real definition, since in linguistic definition, like real definition, observation exists. Then, if observation is considered in nazar, it would necessitate that whenever nazar is mentioned, every time a new definition (hadd jadid) [would arise].
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut, explains the definition of nazar (speculative reasoning) and the nature of basit (simple concepts) in relation to kasb (acquisition of knowledge). The author begins by noting that some who accept rational obligation respond to a previous argument by pointing out that the apparent meaning (dalala) of revealed texts is often only presumptive (zanni), so the necessity of nazar cannot be proven from scripture alone. Hence, the author (Ibn al-Humam) proved it via a rational principle: nazar is a prerequisite (muqaddima) of obligation, and everything prerequisite to an obligation is obligatory. This establishes nazar as wajib rationally.

Then the passage addresses the definition of basit: it is a concept with no parts (plurality). For kasb in the sciences, one must order known premises (tartib) to reach a conclusion. Since basit lacks the multiplicity needed for ordering, it cannot serve as a means (sabab) for acquiring knowledge through nazar. The matn's statement 'la yaqbal al-amal' (it does not accept work) points to this.

However, the author clarifies that this ruling hinges on the definition of nazar itself. If nazar requires sequential ordering of multiple elements (as in a syllogism), then basit cannot be kasb. But some scholars, like Taftazani and the commentator of al-Mawaqif, define nazar simply as 'observation of the intelligible' (mulahazat al-ma'qul), without requiring ordering. In that view, basit can be a sabab because a simple observation suffices. The passage notes that this disagreement is mainly verbal (khilaf lafzi) because it does not affect practical outcomes.

Finally, the author objects to allowing definition by simple concepts, arguing that observation of an essence (mulahazat al-mahiyya) is not considered kasb by consensus. If it were, then linguistic definitions would be considered real definitions, and mere mention of nazar would produce new knowledge—consequences the author deems corrupt.

Key Terms
بسيط (basit): A concept that has no parts (ajza) at all, lacking plurality.
كسب (kasb): Acquisition of knowledge through a process of reasoning (nazar) that involves ordering known premises.
نظر (nazar): Speculative reasoning that leads to knowledge; defined either as requiring ordering (tartib) or as mere observation (mulahaza).
ترتيب (tartib): Sequential ordering of premises in reasoning, necessary for kasb in nazar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the disagreement about basit being kasb is verbal?
A) Because both sides agree that basit cannot be kasb.
B) Because the dispute has no practical consequence on how knowledge is acquired in the sciences.
C) Because the author rejects the observation definition entirely.
D) Because the matn states it is verbal.

Key Takeaway
Whether a simple concept (basit) can be acquired through nazar depends entirely on the definition of nazar; under the Hanafi definition requiring ordering, basit cannot be kasb, and the dispute with Ash'ari scholars is verbal with no practical import.

Mu`arrif and its Three Types in Hanafi Usul
Definition of mu`arrif and its three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify definitions into haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi, and apply the Hanafi condition of coextension to evaluate a proposed definiens.

Core Idea
A definiens must be coextensive—include all instances and exclude all non-instances.

In Hanafi usul, knowledge begins with conception (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). For reasoned conception, we need a method called mu`arrif (definiens). This passage from al-Muslim al-Thubut defines mu`arrif and classifies definitions into three types: real (by essential attributes), formal (by necessary concomitants), and verbal (by a more apparent synonym). It also permits verbal definition by a more general term, a point of debate with other logicians. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for precise legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the coextension condition
Memorize the definition: 'that which prevents the entering from exiting and the exiting from entering.' This means the definiens must apply to every instance of the definiendum (universal) and to nothing else (exclusive).
This is the standard طرد وعكس rule.
2
Distinguish the three types of definition
Haqiqi uses essential attributes (dhatiyyat), rasmi uses necessary concomitants (lazim), and lafzi uses a more apparent synonym. Note that Hanafi usul allows verbal definition by a more general term.
Example: defining 'human' as 'animal' is a verbal definition.
3
Understand the meta-claim about objections
The text states that all objections to definitions are 'claims,' meaning the definer can simply deny the presuppositions. The burden of proof lies on the objector.
This is a strong default position in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the classification to examples
Given a proposed definition, classify it as haqiqi, rasmi, or lafzi and verify if it satisfies the coextension condition.
For fiqh terms, this is a key analytical skill.

ترجمہ :۔ معرف وہ ہے جو داخل کو خارج ہونے سے اور خارج کو داخل ہونے سے روک دے اس لئے معرف کا جامع و مانع ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور تمام اعتراضات جو تعرات پر کئے جاتے ہیں دعاوی ہیں ان کے جواب میں ”لا“ کہنا کافی ہے۔ اور وہ حقیقی ہے اگر تعریف ذاتیات سے ہو اور رکھی ہے اگر لازم کے ذریعہ سے ہو۔ اور تعریف لفظی کہلاتی ہے اگر اس سے زیادہ مشہور واضح اور مرادف لفظ سے ہو۔ اور تعریف لفظی کی عام سے بھی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ اور ذاتی وہ چیز ہے جسکا سمجھنا ذات کے سمجھنے پر موقوف ہو اور کہا گیا ہے کہ ذاتی وہ ہے جو غیر معلل ہو ( یعنی ذاتی وہ جس کا ثبوت

تمهيد: جب مصنف نظر کی تعریف اور وجوب نظر کے بیان سے فارغ ہوئے تو وہ کیا اس طریق کے بیان کرنے کا جس میں نظر واقع ہوتی ہے، چنانچہ یہ معلوم ہے کہ علم تصور ہوگا یا تصدیق اور ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک بدیہی و نظر ہوتا ہے ، پس تصوری نظری کے لئے ایک ایسا طریق نظر چاہئے جس میں نظر کرنے سے تصور نظری کے حصول تک پہنچنا ممکن ہو سکے اس طرح تصدیق نظری کے لئے بھی ایسا طریق نظر چاہئے جس میں نظر کرنے سے تصدیق نظری کے حصول تک پہو نچنا ممکن ہو سکے۔ طریق اول کو معرف کہتے ہیں، اور طریق دوم کو صحت سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔ پھر چونکہ تصدیق اپنے تحقق میں تصور کا محتاج ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس طریق سے بحث کرنا جو موصل بجانب تصور ہو مقدم ہوگا اس طریق کی بحث پر جو موصل بجانب تصدیق ہے اس لئے مصنف نے نظر کے دونوں طریق کو بیان کیا اور معرف کو حجت پر مقدم کیا تا کہ وضع طبع کے موافق ہو جائے تو کہا المعرف ما منع ۔

تشريح قوله المعرف مامنع الوالج من الخروج الخ معرف بالکسر وہ ایسا قول یا طریق کا سب ہے جو معرف بالفتح ، کے افراد میں داخل کو خروج سے اور معرف بالفتح کے افراد سے خارج کو دخول سے منع کرے۔ معنی یہ ہے کہ معرف بالکسر اس حیثیت کا ہو کہ معرف بالفتح بھی اسی پر صادق آئے جس پر معرف بالکسر صادق آتا ہے جس کا مفہوم مطابقی یہ ہے کہ معرف معرف کے جمیع افراد کو جامع ہو۔ اور اسی طرح معرف بالکسر بھی اسی پر صادق آئے جس پر معرف بافتح صادق آرہا ہے جس کا مفہوم مطابقی یہ ہے کہ معرف معرف میں غیر افراد کے دخول کو مانع ہو۔ اس مفہوم کی طرف ماتن نے اپنے قول فیجب الطر دو العکس سے اشارہ کیا ہے۔ حاصل تعریف :- یہ ہے کہ معرف بالکسر معرف بالفتح کے ساتھ صدق میں مساوی ہوگا یعنی معرف ہر اس چیز پر صادق آئے گا جس پر معرف صادق آتا ہے اور جس پر معرف صادق آتا ہے اس پر معرف بھی صادق آئے گا۔ چونکہ معرف و معرف میں تساوی ہے جو تلازم فی الثبوت اور تلازم فی الانتفاء کو مستلزم ہے۔ یعنی جن افراد پر معرف صادق آئے گا معرف بھی صادق آئے گا اور جن افراد پر معرف
The matn of al-Muslim: The definiens (mu`arrif) is that which prevents the entering from exiting and the exiting from entering, so [it must] include and exclude. All objections to definitions are claims, and it suffices to answer them with denial. It is real (haqiqi) if by essential attributes (dhatiyyat), and formal (rasmi) if by necessary concomitant (lazim). And it is called verbal (lafzi) if by a more apparent synonym. And it is permitted with a more general (term). And the essential (dhati) is what is understood in the understanding of the essence, and it is said: that which is not caused (ghayr mu`allal), and it is refuted by possibility (imkan) since there is no possibility through another.

Translation: The definiens is what prevents the inner from exiting and the outer from entering; therefore the definiens must be universal and exclusive. All objections made to definitions are claims; in answer to them, saying 'no' is sufficient. And it is real if the definition is by essential attributes, and formal if by a necessary concomitant. And it is called verbal if from a more famous, clear, and synonymous word. And it is permitted to use a more general (term) for verbal definition. And the essential is that which understanding depends on understanding the essence, and it is said that the essential is that which is not caused (i.e., the essential is that whose existence for an essence is not through a cause other than the essence itself). But this definition is refuted by possibility (imkan) because possibility's existence for the possible is not through an intermediary (cause)?

Preamble: When the author finished with the definition of nazar and the obligation of nazar, he proceeded to describe the method in which nazar occurs. It is known that knowledge is either conception (tasawwur) or assent (tasdiq), and each of these is either intuitive (badihi) or reasoned (nazari). For reasoned conception, a method of nazar is needed by which through nazar one can attain reasoned conception. Similarly, for reasoned assent, a method of nazar is needed by which through nazar one can attain reasoned assent. The first method is called definiens (mu`arrif), and the second method is called proof (hujja). Then, because assent in its realization depends on conception, discussing the method that leads to conception is prior to discussing the method that leads to assent. Therefore the author mentioned both methods and gave priority to definiens over proof to accord with the natural order. So he said: al-mu`arrif is that which prevents...

Elucidation: His statement: 'al-mu`arrif is that which prevents the entering from exiting, etc.' – mu`arrif (with kasr) is a statement or method that prevents the entering of what is inside the individual of the definiendum (mu`arrif with fatha) from exiting, and the exiting of what is outside the individuals of the definiendum from entering. The meaning is that mu`arrif (with kasr) should be such that mu`arrif (with fatha) also applies to what mu`arrif (with kasr) applies to; its connotative meaning is that the definiens includes all individuals of the definiendum. Similarly, mu`arrif (with kasr) should apply to what mu`arrif (with fatha) applies to; its connotative meaning is that the definiens prevents the entrance of non-individuals. The matn author indicated this meaning by his saying 'so [it must] include and exclude.' The conclusion of the definition is that mu`arrif (with kasr) and mu`arrif (with fatha) are coextensive in application, i.e., mu`arrif applies to everything that mu`arrif applies to, and mu`arrif applies to that to which mu`arrif applies. Because there is equality between mu`arrif and mu`arrif, which entails concomitance in existence and concomitance in non-existence: that is, to which individuals mu`arrif applies, mu`arrif also applies, and to which individuals mu`arrif applies,
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage defines the definiens (mu`arrif) and its types in Hanafi usul. The matn states that the definiens must prevent the inner from exiting and the outer from entering, meaning it must be universal (including all instances) and exclusive (excluding all non-instances). All objections to definitions can be answered by denying the presuppositions. The definition is classified as haqiqi (real) if it uses essential attributes (dhatiyyat), rasmi (formal) if it uses necessary concomitants, and lafzi (verbal) if it uses a more apparent synonym. The commentator adds that verbal definition may also be given by a more general term. The 'essential' (dhati) is defined paradoxically: it is what is understood when the essence is understood, or what is uncaused – but the latter definition is refuted by the concept of possibility (imkan) because possibility is not caused by another. The commentator then provides a preamble explaining the logical sequence: knowledge is either conception or assent, each intuitive or reasoned. For reasoned conception, the method is mu`arrif (definition); for reasoned assent, it is hujja (proof). Since assent depends on conception, definition precedes proof. The tashrih elaborates on the coextensiveness of the definiens and definiendum, explaining that the definiens must be equal in application, leading to mutual entailment.

Key Terms
المعرف (al-mu`arrif): The definiens; a statement or method that prevents the entering of the interior individuals from exiting and the exterior individuals from entering, i.e., it is coextensive with the definiendum.
الذاتي (al-dhati): The essential (attribute); what is understood in the understanding of the essence, or what is not caused (ghayr mu`allal).
تعريف لفظي (ta`rif lafzi): Verbal definition; explaining a word by a more apparent synonym or even a more general term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a correct definiens according to the matn?
A) It must prevent the entering from exiting.
B) It must be a single word.
C) It must be coextensive.
D) All objections can be answered by denial.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definiens must be coextensive with the definiendum; definitions can be real, formal, or verbal, and objections can be met by denial.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

8 min
Three Types of Definition in Usul: Haqiqi, Rasmi, and Lafzi
Classification of definitions and terminology differences between usul and logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi definitions according to Hanafi usul, and identify the terminological differences between usuliyyun and logicians.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, haqiqi and rasmi are opposites; logicians oppose haqiqi to lafzi.

Definitions (taʿrīf) are fundamental to legal theory: they shape how we understand the terms used in the sources. This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary not only classifies definitions into three types but also highlights a crucial terminological difference between the usul scholars and the logicians. Understanding these classifications will sharpen your ability to evaluate definitions in legal reasoning and avoid common confusions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of objections to definitions
The passage begins by noting that objections to definitions are essentially claims that require proof. This sets the stage for why precise classification matters: a proper definition must be defensible against objections like being too broad or too narrow.
Note the shift from general methodology to specific classification.
2
Memorize the three types of definition in usul
The author explicitly lists haqiqi (by essential properties), rasmi (by accidents), and lafzi (by synonym). Commit these categories and their examples to memory.
Example: haqiqi = 'man is a rational animal'; rasmi = 'man is laughing'; lafzi = 'ghadanfar is asad'.
3
Analyze the purpose of each definition type
Haqiqi gives complete conceptualization of the essence. Rasmi gives partial conceptualization via a distinguishing accident. Lafzi merely provides a synonym to clarify the term.
This teleological approach is key to the usuli classification.
4
Compare usuli vs. logician classifications
Logicians divide definitions into haqiqi (producing an unattained mental form) and lafzi (distinguishing an attained form). For logicians, rasmi is a subcategory of haqiqi. For usuliyyun, rasmi is opposite to haqiqi.
This difference arises because usuliyyun focus on the completeness of conceptualization, while logicians focus on the mental operation.
5
Apply the classification to legal examples
Consider how you would define legal terms like 'wudu' or 'salah'. Decide whether a given definition is haqiqi (essential), rasmi (by accidents like conditions), or lafzi (synonym). This skill is essential for istinbat.
The choice of definition type can affect legal reasoning.

Source Text

ضروری ہے تا کہ اس دلیل کے کسی مقدمہ معینہ پر منع نقض اور معارضہ وارد کیا جا سکے .. ہاں البتہ تعریف دعاوی ضمیہ پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے جیسے یہ دھوئی کہ یہ تعریف مثلا حدی ہے رسمی ہے یا تعریف جامع و مانع ہے وغیرہ پس ان دعاوی ضمنیہ کے پیش نظر تعریف پر منوع ثلثہ مذکورہ متوجہ ہو سکتے ہیں لیکن منع مجرد نا کافی ہے بلکہ منع کے ساتھ شاہد بھی ضروری ہے تا کہ تعریف کا دروازہ بند نہ ہو جائے ۔ اور جب منع شاہد کے ساتھ وارد ہوگا تو وہ نقض کی طرف اور عدم جامعیت، مانعیت کے دعوی کی طرف راجع ہوتا ہے اسلئے مصنف نے کہا و جمیع الا سرادات علی التعریف دعاوی ۔ یعنی تمام اعتراضات جو تعریف وارد کئے جاتے ہیں وہ در حقیقت دعوے ہوتے ہیں اور دعاوی ضمنیہ کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے وارد کئے جاتے ہیں اس لئے معترض کے لئے لازم ہے کہ اپنے دعوی یا اعتراض پر دلیل و شاہد بھی پیش کرے مثال کے طور پر معترض تعریف پر یہ اعتراض کرے کہ یہ تعریف حدی نہیں ہو سکتی، یار کمی نہیں ہو سکتی یا جامع ومانع نہیں ہے وغیرہ اور اس پر شاہد و دلیل نہ پیش کرے تو ان اعتراضات کے جواب میں منع کافی ہے یعنی تعریف کرنے والا یہ کہے گا کہ اے معترض ! تم نے جو اعتراض وارد کیا ہے ہم اس پر منع وارد کرتے ہیں یا ہم اسے تسلیم نہیں کرتے جیتک تم اس منع کے ساتھ دلیل نہ پیش کرو گے اور اگر تعریف کنندہ تعریف پر اعتراض کے جواب میں منع کے ساتھ شاہد بھی ذکر کر دیتا ہے تو یہ زیادہ نفع بخش ہوگا گو کہ صرف منع بھی کافی ہے۔

قوله : وهو حقيقى ان كان بالذاتيات الخ
یہاں سے مصنف معرف کی تقسیم کرنا چاہتے ہیں اس لئے کہا وھو حقیقی ۔ یعنی اجمالاً مجموعی طور پر معرف کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔ حقیقی ، رسمی لفظی ، تعریف حقیقی وہ ہے جوٹی کی تعریف ذاتیات کے ذریعہ سے ہو جیسے انسان کی تعریف حیوان ناطق ہے۔ رسمی وہ ہے جوشی تعریف اس کے لوازم کے ذریعہ سے ہو جیسے انسان کی تعریف کا تب سے اور شراب کی تعریف ہر اس بہنے والی چیز سے کی جاوے جو جھاگ لائے۔ تعریف لفظی اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو معرف کے مرادف اور اس سے لفظ سے ہو جیسے غضنفر کی تعریف اسد سے اور عقار کی تعریف خمر ہے۔ واضح رہے کہ منطقی کے نزدیک تعریف لفظی تعریف حقیقی کا مقابل ہوتی ہے پس حقیقی کے اندر حدور تم دونوں شامل ہوتی ہیں مگر اصولی کے نزدیک حقیقی کا مقابل رسمی ہوتی ہے لفظی نہیں ، اس لئے مصنف نے رسمی کو حقیقی کے مقابل رکھا ہے۔ اس کی مزید تفصیل یہ ہے کہ منطق کی اصطلاح میں حقیقی کا اطلاق کبھی لفظی کے مقابل ہوتا ہے اس تقدیر پر حقیقی بولی جاتی ہے ایسی چیز پر جس کے ذریعہ مٹی کی صورت غیر حاصلہ کو حاصل کیا جائے اور کبھی حقیقی کا اطلاق تعریف بحسب الحقیقہ پر ہوتا ہے جو تعریف بحسب الاسم کے مقابل ہوتی ہے جس میں معرف موجود کی حقیقت کی طرف وصول مقصود ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ مناطقہ تعریف کی اس طرح تقسیم کرتے ہیں کہ تعریف یا تو ذہن میں صورت غیر حاصلہ حاصل کرائیگی یا صورت حاصلہ کا اپنے ماعدا اسے تمیز کا افادہ کرے گی بر تقدیر ثانی وہ تعریف لفظی ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا فائدہ یہ ہوتا ہے کہ معنی معین کے بالمقابل لفظ کی معرفت ہوتی ہے جیسے الغضنفر حوالاسد ۔ پھر لفظی کبھی مفرد ہوتی ہے جیسے مثال مذکور میں اور کبھی مرکب ہوتا ہے جیسے وجود کی تعریف الثابت العین وغیرہ الفاظ مرکبہ سے کرنا ، اور بر تقدیر اول (یعنی تعریف صورت غیر حاصلہ ذہن میں حاصل ہونے کا افادہ کرے گی ) تو اس کی بھی دوصورت ہوتی ہے کیونکہ ذہن میں یا تو ایسی صورت حاصل ہوگی جس کا وجود نفس الامر کے اعتبار سے جانا گیا ہو یانہیں برصورت اول تعریف بحسب الحقیقہ ہوتی ہے جیسے انسان کی تعریف حیوان ناطق ہے ۔ اور برصورت ثانی (یعنی اگر ایسی صورت کا علم حاصل ہو جس کا موجود ہو تانفس الامر کے اعتبار سے نہیں جانا گیا ہو بلکہ اسکا وجود صرف باعتبار اصطلاح دو ماہیات اعتباریہ میں سے ہونا معلوم ہو تو وہ تعریف بحسب الاسم ( تعریف رسمی ) ہے جیسے کلمہ کی تعریف ”لفظ وضع لمعنی مفرد سے کرنا۔
اس تفصیل سے ظاہر ہے کہ رسمی حقیقی میں داخل ہے اور لفظی حقیقی کے مقابل ہے۔ کا مناطقہ کا مذہب ہے اسکے برخلاف اصولیین کی اصطلاح میں حدوہ ہے جو مناطقہ کے نزدیک معرف ہے اس لئے اصولیین اس طرح تقسیم کرتے ہیں کہ حد سے یا تو صورت غیر حاصلہ کے حاصل کرنے کا قصد کیا جائے گا یا نہیں بلکہ خزانہ ذہن میں محفوظ معنی کے حاضر کرنے کا قصد کیا جائے گا بر تقدیر اول یا توشی کے ذات کی صورت حاصل ہوگی یا اس کے وجوہ میں سے کسی وجہ کی صورت حاصل ہوگی اول حقیقی ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے شئی کا تصور بالکنہ حاصل ہوتا ہے اور ثانی رسمی ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے شئی کا تصور بالوجہ حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ اور بر تقدیر ثانی (یعنی ظرف ذہن میں موجود و مخزون معنی کا احضار مقصود ہو ) تو لفظی
It is necessary so that denial, refutation, and opposition can be directed at a specific premise of that proof. Yes, but definition consists of implied claims, such as the claim that this definition is, for example, a comprehensive definition (haddī) or a descriptive definition (rasmī), or that the definition is comprehensive and exclusive, etc. So with consideration of these implied claims, the three mentioned objections can be directed at the definition. But mere denial is insufficient; rather, with denial a proof is also necessary so that the door of definition is not closed. And when denial is accompanied by proof, it refers back to refutation and to the claim of lack of comprehensiveness or exclusivity. Therefore, the author said: 'And all the objections to the definition are claims.' That is, all the objections that are made to the definition are in reality claims, and they are made with an eye to the implied claims. Therefore, it is necessary for the objector to also present evidence and proof for his claim or objection. For example, if the objector makes an objection to the definition that this definition cannot be comprehensive (haddī), or cannot be a description (rasmī), or is not comprehensive and exclusive, etc., and he does not present proof and evidence for it, then in response to these objections, denial is sufficient. That is, the definer will say: 'O objector! The objection you have made, we deny it, or we do not accept it, until you present evidence along with this denial.' And if the definer, in response to the objection to the definition, mentions a proof along with denial, it will be more beneficial, even though mere denial is also sufficient.

His statement: 'And it is haqiqi if it is by essential properties, etc.' From here, the author intends to divide the defined thing (muʿarraf). Thus he said: 'And it is haqiqi.' That is, in summary, the defined thing has three types collectively: haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi. The haqiqi definition is that by which a thing is defined through its essential properties (dhātīyāt), like the definition of man as 'rational animal'. The rasmi definition is that by which a thing is defined through its accidents (lawāzim), like the definition of man as 'laughing' and the definition of wine as 'every flowing thing that froths'. The lafzi definition is called that which is a synonym of the defined thing (muʿarraf) and from its word, like the definition of 'ghadanfar' as 'asad' (lion) and the definition of 'ʿuqār' as 'khamr' (wine). It should be clear that according to the logician (manṭiqī), the lafzi definition is opposite to the haqiqi definition; thus the haqiqi includes both the complete and incomplete definitions (ḥadd and rasm). But according to the usuli, the opposite of haqiqi is rasmi, not lafzi. Therefore, the author placed rasmi opposite to haqiqi. Its further detail is that in the terminology of logic, 'haqiqi' is sometimes used in opposition to 'lafzi'; in this case, 'haqiqi' is applied to something through which an unattained form (ṣūra ghayr ḥāṣila) is attained. And sometimes 'haqiqi' is applied to the definition according to reality (taʿrif bi-ḥasab al-ḥaqīqa), which is opposite to the definition according to name (taʿrif bi-ḥasab al-ism), in which the goal is to reach the reality of the defined existing thing. Since the logicians divide definition as: either it will cause an unattained form to be attained in the mind, or it will provide the benefit of distinguishing an attained form from what is other than it. In the second case, it is a lafzi definition because its benefit is that knowledge of the word is obtained in comparison to a specific meaning, like 'al-ghadanfar huwa al-asad'. Then lafzi is sometimes simple (mufrad), like in the mentioned example, and sometimes compound (murakkab), like defining existence as 'al-thābit al-ʿayn', etc. from compound words. And in the first case (i.e., the definition benefits the attainment of an unattained form in the mind), it also has two forms: because in the mind either such a form will be attained whose existence is known according to reality (nafs al-amr), or not. In the first case, it is a definition according to reality, like the definition of man as 'rational animal'. And in the second case (i.e., if knowledge is obtained of such a form whose existence is not known according to reality, but its existence is known only by way of terminological convention (iṣṭilāḥ) and from among the conventional entities), then it is a definition according to name (taʿrif bi-ḥasab al-ism), which is the rasmi definition, like defining 'kalima' as 'a word placed for a meaning singly'.
From this detail it is clear that 'rasmi' is included in 'haqiqi', and 'lafzi' is opposite to 'haqiqi'. That is the doctrine of the logicians. In contrast, the terminology of the usuliyyun is such that 'ḥadd' and 'rasm'—which according to logicians are the defined thing (muʿarraf)—are divided by the usuliyyun as follows: from 'ḥadd' either the intention is to attain an unattained form, or not; rather, the intention is to bring to mind the meaning preserved in the treasury of the mind. In the first case, either the form of the essence of the thing will be attained, or the form of some aspect among its aspects. The first is 'haqiqi' because it provides a complete conceptualization (taṣawwur bil-kunh) of the thing, and the second is 'rasmi' because it provides a conceptualization by aspect (taṣawwur bil-wajh). And in the second case (i.e., the intended is the summoning of the meaning present and stored in the mind), then it is 'lafzi'.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the classification of definitions (taʿrīf) in usul al-fiqh. It begins by discussing the nature of objections to definitions—that they are essentially claims requiring proof—and then transitions to the types of definition as presented by the author of the matn. The commentary clarifies that according to usuliyyun, there are three types: haqiqi (definition by essential properties, e.g., 'man is a rational animal'), rasmi (definition by accidents, e.g., 'man is laughing'), and lafzi (definition by synonym, e.g., 'ghadanfar is asad'). It highlights a key terminological difference: logicians (manṭiqiyyūn) consider lafzi as the opposite of haqiqi, whereas usuliyyun consider rasmi as the opposite. The passage then elaborates on the logical classification: definitions either produce an unattained mental form or distinguish an attained form; the latter is lafzi. Among those that produce unattained forms, if the form corresponds to reality, it is definition according to reality (haqiqi); if it is conventional, it is definition according to name (rasmi). Finally, it contrasts the logicians' two-fold division (haqiqi-lafzi) with the usuliyyun's three-fold division (haqiqi, rasmi, lafzi) based on the purpose of the definition: attaining complete conceptualization, partial conceptualization, or merely summoning a known meaning.

Key Terms
تعریف حقیقی (taʿrīf ḥaqīqī): A definition that uses the essential properties (dhātīyāt) of a thing to provide complete knowledge of its essence, e.g., 'man is a rational animal'.
تعریف رسمی (taʿrīf rasmī): A definition that uses accidents (lawāzim) of a thing to provide partial knowledge, e.g., 'man is laughing' or 'wine is every flowing thing that froths'.
تعریف لفظی (taʿrīf lafẓī): A definition that uses a synonym of the defined term, e.g., 'ghadanfar is asad' (lion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to usul al-fiqh, which type of definition gives complete knowledge of the essence of a thing?
A) Haqiqi definition
B) Rasmi definition
C) Lafzi definition
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The classification of definitions into haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi differs between usuliyyun and logicians; in Hanafi usul, haqiqi and rasmi are directly opposed.

Verbal Definition (Lafzi) and the Use of More General Terms
Explains lafzi definition and dispute over defining by a broader term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of definition in Hanafi usul and evaluate the dispute regarding defining by a more general term (a'am).

Core Idea
A verbal definition clarifies a word by a more apparent synonym; some scholars allow using a more general term, others restrict it.

In Hanafi usul, definitions are classified into real (haqiqi), formal (rasmi), and verbal (lafzi). This lesson focuses on verbal definition and a key debate: can you define a word using a more general term? The answer depends on whether the definition serves a conceptual or assertive purpose. We will unpack the dispute and its implications for legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of definition
According to usul scholars, definitions are divided into haqiqi, rasmi, and lafzi. Verbal definition is clarified by a more apparent synonym.
The logicians have a different classification, but usul scholars adapted it.
2
Understand the concept of verbal definition
Verbal definition (lafzi) clarifies a word by a more apparent synonym, e.g., defining 'ghadanfar' by 'asad' (both mean lion).
The synonym must be more apparent (azhar) than the defined word.
3
Recognize the dispute over using a more general term
Some scholars allow definition by a more general term (a'am) only in verbal definitions; others allow it in both verbal and real definitions. The text argues the specification to verbal is misplaced.
The dispute is about the principle of defining by a broader term, not just the type of definition.
4
Distinguish the purpose: tasawwuri vs tasdiqi
Verbal definition can aim at either conceptual understanding (tasawwuri) — depicting the meaning — or assertive confirmation (tasdiqi) — confirming the word-meaning correspondence.
The author concludes both are possible depending on intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے۔ الغرض اصولین نے اطلاق حقیقی میں اور تعریف رسمی کو حقیقی کا مقابل قرار دینے میں منطقیہ کی مخالفت کی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک معرف کی اقسام اولیہ حقیقی ، رسمی اور لفظی کہلاتی ہیں پس لفظی حقیقی اور رسمی میں جاری ہو سکتی ہے جب ان دونوں پر دور طاری ہو حالانکہ لفظی بظاہر حقیقی و رسمی کی قسم ہے۔ قوله - قد اجيز بالاعم" یعنی لفظی تعریف میں چونکہ لفظ کی توضیح اس کے مرادف اظہر لفظ سے کی جاتی ہے اس لئے اس کی تعریف و توضیح عام سے جائز قرار دی گئی ہے جیسے معدن کی تعریف نسبت سے اور غضنفر کی تعریف اسد سے کی جائے ۔ مگر لفظی کے ساتھ یہ تخصیص بے محل ہے کیونکہ جنہوں نے عام سے تعریف کو جائز قرار دیا ہے ان کے نزدیک لفظی کی طرح حقیقی بھی عام سے جائز ہے اور جو عام سے تعریف کو جائز قرار نہیں دیتے ان کے نزدیک حقیقی و لفظی ہر ایک میں عام سے تعریف صحیح نہیں ہے۔
یہاں یہ بات ذہن نشین رہے کہ تعریف لفظی سے صورت حاصلہ کی تمیز مقصود یعنی اس کا مقصود اصلی ذہن میں حاصل شدہ معنی کی معرفت کہ اس کے مقابلہ میں لفظ کو وضع کیا جائے اور تصدیق بھی کہا جائے کہ لفظ مثلا اس معنی کیلئے ہے اس تقدیر پر لفظی مطالب تصدیقیہ سے ہوگی چنانچہ اسی لئے کہا گیا کہ لفظی سے احضار مقصود ہوتا ہے بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ تعریف لفظی مطالب تصدیقیہ سے ہے۔ اور اگر لفظی سے معانی مخزونہ کے درمیان لفظ کے مدلول کا بیان اور لفظ اشہر سے معنی کی تصویر مقصود ہو تو اس وقت لفظی مطالب تصوریہ سے ہوگی اس لئے کہ لفظی سے لفظ کے مدلول کا بیان و تصویر ہوتا ہے بعض لوگوں نے کہا ہے کہ تعریف لفظی مطالب تصوریہ کے قبیل سے ہے حق یہ ہے کہ دونوں احتمال کے اعتبار سے دونوں مطالب سے ہو سکتی ہے۔
The purpose: The usul scholars opposed the logicians in applying 'real' (haqiqi) and making 'formal' (rasmi) definition a counterpart of 'real'. Thus, according to them, the primary types of definition are called real, formal, and verbal (lafzi). So verbal can operate in real and formal when a vicious circle occurs on both, although verbal is apparently a type of real and formal. His statement: 'It has been permitted by the more general [term]' means that in verbal definition, since the word is clarified by its more apparent synonym, its definition and clarification by the more general is deemed permissible, like defining 'mail' (ma'din) by 'metal' (ribsat) and 'lion' (ghadanfar) by 'lion' (asad). But this specification to verbal is misplaced because those who permit definition by the more general, according to them, real also is permissible by the more general like verbal, and those who do not permit definition by the more general, according to them, in both real and verbal definition by the more general is not correct.
Here it should be borne in mind that the purpose of verbal definition is to distinguish the acquired form, i.e., its primary purpose is to recognize the meaning obtained in the mind so that the word is placed in contrast to it, and also it is said to be tasdiqi (assertive) that the word is for that meaning. On this assumption, verbal definition will be from the assertive demand. Therefore, because verbal brings about the intended meaning, some people said that verbal definition is from the assertive demand. And if by verbal the intended is the explanation of the word's signification among stored meanings and the depiction of the meaning by a more famous word, then verbal definition will be from the conceptual (tasawwuri) demand, because through verbal the signification and depiction of the word's meaning occurs. Some people said that verbal definition is of the category of conceptual demand. The truth is that, considering both possibilities, it can be from both demands.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage discusses the classification of definitions (ta'rif) into three types: real (haqiqi), formal (rasmi), and verbal (lafzi). The author, commenting on the matn, explains that usul scholars differ from logicians in their classification. They consider verbal definition as a type that can be applied when a vicious circle occurs in real or formal definitions. The main point is the permissibility of defining something by a more general term (a'am). Some scholars allow it only in verbal definitions, while others allow it in both real and verbal. The author then clarifies the purpose of verbal definition: it can serve either an assertive (tasdiqi) purpose—to confirm that a word corresponds to a meaning—or a conceptual (tasawwuri) purpose—to depict the meaning through a more famous word. Both are possible depending on intention.

Key Terms
لفظی (lafẓī): Verbal definition: clarifying a word by its more apparent synonym
عام (ʿāmm): A more general term used to define a specific word

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because verbal definitions are less precise than real definitions
B) Because verbal definitions inherently involve clarifying a word by a more familiar term, and that term may be more general
C) Because real definitions cannot use general terms at all
D) Because the logicians forbid it in real definitions

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition clarifies by a more apparent synonym; the permissibility of using a more general term applies to all definitions, not just verbal ones.
